Here's how to protect your small business against a cyber attack"},{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#webpage","url":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html","name":"The Most Effective Ways To Protect Your Small Business From Cyber Attacks - Small Business Trends","isPartOf":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#website"},"primaryImageOfPage":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#primaryimage"},"datePublished":"2017-01-13T13:30:20+00:00","dateModified":"2021-04-13T13:07:41+00:00","description":"Small businesses are even more prone to cyber threats becuase they're weaker on defense. Here's how to protect your small business against a cyber attack","breadcrumb":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#breadcrumb"},"inLanguage":"en-US","potentialAction":[{"@type":"ReadAction","target":["https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html"]}]},{"@type":"BreadcrumbList","@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#breadcrumb","itemListElement":[{"@type":"ListItem","position":1,"name":"The Most Effective Ways To Protect Your Small Business From Cyber Attacks"}]},{"@type":["Article","NewsArticle"],"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#article","isPartOf":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#webpage"},"author":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#/schema/person/a08ac3acef91b65ea6a24e071bf9e67a"},"headline":"The Most Effective Ways To Protect Your Small Business From Cyber Attacks","datePublished":"2017-01-13T13:30:20+00:00","dateModified":"2021-04-13T13:07:41+00:00","mainEntityOfPage":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#webpage"},"wordCount":1486,"publisher":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#organization"},"image":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#primaryimage"},"thumbnailUrl":"https://media.smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/shutterstock_507108913.jpg","articleSection":["Technology Trends"],"inLanguage":"en-US","copyrightYear":"2017","copyrightHolder":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#organization"},"articleBody":"Okay, I\u2019m going to start with a question. What would happen if a hacker decided to launch a cyber attack against your business? Would they be successful? Would they easily gain access to your company\u2019s sensitive information? Or would their attempt fall flat? Believe it or not, cyber security isn\u2019t just a concern for large businesses. It\u2019s something that small business owners need to pay attention to. Consider these statistics about Small Business Security: 43 percent of cyber attacks target small business. Only 14 percent of small businesses rate their ability to mitigate cyber risks, vulnerabilities and attacks as highly effective. 60 percent of small companies go out of business within six months of a cyber attack. 48 percent of data security breaches are caused by acts of malicious intent. Human error or system failure account for the rest. If you\u2019re a small business owner, you can\u2019t ignore these statistics. You don\u2019t want your business to suffer because you didn\u2019t take the appropriate steps to protect it. You have worked way too hard to allow your company to be threatened by a\u00a0hacker, right?\u00a0In this post, you will learn why it\u2019s important to focus on cyber security. You will also learn how you can protect your business. Why Should Small Businesses Be Concerned With Cyber Security? I know what you\u2019re thinking. You\u2019re thinking that your business is so small, nobody would ever want to hack it. It\u2019s easy to think that a small business would never have to deal with cyber security issues. Makes sense, right? Usually when you hear about a company being hacked, it\u2019s a major brand like Target or Sony. But these aren\u2019t the only targets. It may sound hard to believe, but hackers target small businesses too. You just don\u2019t hear about it because the media isn\u2019t going to report on hacks involving small businesses. There are several reasons why a hacker might go after a small business... Small Businesses Don\u2019t Take Cyber Security Seriously Let\u2019s face it. Most small business owners don\u2019t take cyber security seriously. They think that they\u2019re too small to get a hacker\u2019s attention. However, this is one of the main reasons why a small business might get hacked. Hackers know that most small business owners don\u2019t invest in cyber security. Why? Because small business owners tend to think they have nothing worth stealing. This makes them an easy target. Chances are, you do have something that hackers want: customer payment information. That brings me to my next point... You Have Information That Hackers Want Your business may not be as big as Target or Starbucks ... but it doesn\u2019t matter. You do take payment for your products and services, right? That means you have something that hackers want. You have your customers\u2019 payment information. You have your employees' information. The Council of Better Business Bureaus found that 7.4 percent of small business owners have been defrauded. As a business owner, you have customer and employee information. This information is as valuable as gold to hackers. If your system isn\u2019t secure, these hackers could have access to payment information and social security numbers. It\u2019s your job to make sure that this information is protected. How to Protect Your Small Business Against A Cyber Attack Okay, so I\u2019ve showed you that being a small business doesn\u2019t necessarily mean that you can\u2019t get hacked. But if you\u2019re smart --- and I know you are --- you\u2019re probably wondering how you can protect your company\u2019s information. That\u2019s what the next section of this post is about. Get Cyber Security Insurance Insurance! It\u2019s not just for your car, house or medical bills. You can also get insurance for your business. As a matter of fact, every company should carry some type of business insurance. But, there is also cyber security insurance. If you\u2019re a small business, you need this. Sure, we all hope that security breaches won\u2019t happen. But hope isn\u2019t good enough. You need to make sure your business is covered. Cyber liability insurance is designed to protect your business from various cyber security threats. If there is a security breach, and your company is held liable, you may end up having to pay out tons of money in a lawsuit. This can cripple most small businesses. If you have cyber liability insurance, you won\u2019t have to worry about this. If you buy the right type of insurance, your legal costs will be covered. Develop A Password Strategy Many cyber security attacks happen because the passwords your employees use are way too simple. If your team isn\u2019t educated, it\u2019s possible that they\u2019re using passwords that are way too easy to hack. It happens all the time. That\u2019s why you need to implement an effective password strategy. You may not be able to stop every single attack, but you can certainly slow down a persistent hacker. If your system isn\u2019t easy to hack, it could discourage the attacker. They will move on to another small business owner who isn\u2019t as smart as you are! Fortunately, this is pretty easy. You should make sure that your team members are required to create passwords that include a combination of uppercase and lowercase letters, along with numbers and symbols. Yes, I know this might be a pain, but the security your company will have is worth it. Also, you should require your employees to reset their passwords at least once a month. Use Virtual Data Rooms (VDR) Virtual data rooms are a great way to keep your company\u2019s information secure. They make it easier for your employees to share sensitive data. A virtual data room is an online repository where your company can store data. They\u2019re usually used with financial transactions. It\u2019s very hard for a hacker to get to information that is stored in a VDR. There are many types of information that a company might store in a VDR: Financial information Legal documentation Tax paperwork Intellectual property information VDR\u2019s are a great way to ensure that your sensitive information is being kept safe. Speak With An Expert Yes, I know you don\u2019t want to do it. But you should. Paying an IT security consultant might seem to be a little expensive. But it\u2019s a great investment. If your house sprung a leak and water was building up in your kitchen, would you try to fix it yourself? Probably not. You would probably call a plumber, right? Why? Because if you\u2019re like most of us, you don\u2019t know the first thing about plumbing. The same principle applies to IT security. If you\u2019re concerned about cyber security, you should consider speaking with an IT security expert. An IT security consultant can take a look at your business and determine the best course of action when it comes to protecting it from cyber attacks. An IT security consultant can identify areas where your company is vulnerable to cyber attacks. They can make recommendations that will help you keep your business safe. When it comes to cyber security, you can never be too careful. If it\u2019s in your budget, hire an expert. You\u2019ll be glad you did. Beware Of Internal Threats This may be a surprise, but most of the cyber security issues that happen are the result of someone inside the company. It\u2019s not something most business owners want to think about, but it\u2019s totally true. Here\u2019s a hard truth: 55 percent of all cyber attacks come from inside the organization. 31.5 percent are done by malicious employees. 23.5 percent are done by company insiders who mistakenly leave the company vulnerable to an attack. Protecting your company means looking within the organization. It\u2019s easy to assume that a cyber attack is going to come from an outside force. But it\u2019s not true. You have to focus on the people inside your company just as much as people outside your company. Make sure that you are keeping an eye on your authorization requirements. Be careful when you\u2019re deciding which employees should have access to sensitive data. This will help you prevent \u201cinternal hacks.\u201d Don\u2019t feel guilty for watching your employees\u2019 activities; as the owner of your business, it\u2019s your duty to ensure that you and your team are being protected. I get it. You don\u2019t want to micromanage. The key is to find the balance between being safe and being big brother. It\u2019s different for every company, but if you work at it, you will find that balance. Summing It All Up If you\u2019re a small business owner, you need to take your cyber security seriously. Don\u2019t assume that your company isn\u2019t a target just because you\u2019re not a big business. You owe it to yourself, your employees and your customers to make sure that your business is secure. Preventing cyber attacks should be one of your top priorities. If you take the right steps, you won\u2019t have to worry about endangering your business. class="clear"></div></div></div><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-178"></span><hr class="clear"><span class="full-span-featured-image"><img width="850" height="476" src="https://smallbiztrends.com/ezoimgfmt/media.smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/shutterstock_507108913-850x476.jpg?ezimgfmt=ng%3Awebp%2Fngcb12%2Frs%3Adevice%2Frscb12-1" class="attachment-general_850w_image Here's how to protect your small business against a cyber attack" ezimgfmt="rs rscb12 src ng ngcb12" loading="eager" srcset="" sizes=""></span><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-179"></span><span class="ezoic-ad box-3 box-3179 adtester-container adtester-container-179" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-box-3" style="min-height: 90px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-box-3-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; min-height: 90px; min-width: 728px;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CPvDxrf-pPQCFYfqZAod7nkLjA"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-3_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-3_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-3_0" width="728" height="90" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="3" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"><div class="entry"><div class="entry-wrap"><p>Okay, Im going to start with a question.</p><p>What would happen if a hacker decided to launch a cyber attack against your business? Would they be successful? Would they easily gain access to your companys sensitive information? Or would their attempt fall flat?</p><p>Believe it or not, cyber security isnt just a concern for large businesses. Its something that small business owners need to pay attention to.</p><p>Consider these <a href="https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/cyber-security-statistics-small-business.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">statistics about Small Business Security</a>:</p><ul><li>43 percent of cyber attacks target small business.</li><li>Only 14 percent of small businesses rate their ability to mitigate cyber risks, vulnerabilities and attacks as highly effective.</li><li>60 percent of small companies go out of business within six months of a cyber attack.</li><li>48 percent of data security breaches are caused by acts of malicious intent. Human error or system failure account for the rest.</li></ul><p>If youre a small business owner, you cant ignore these statistics. You dont want your business to suffer because you didnt take the appropriate steps to protect it.</p><p>You have worked way too hard to allow your company to be threatened by a&nbsp;hacker, right?&nbsp;In this post, you will learn why its important to focus on cyber security. You will also learn how you can protect your business.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad9" id="quads-ad9" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-106"></span><span class="ezoic-ad banner-1 banner-1106 adtester-container adtester-container-106" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-banner-1" style="min-height: 280px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-banner-1-0" ezaw="336" ezah="280" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 280px; min-width: 336px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CIiDsbb-pPQCFQzcWwodfpMDzQ"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-banner-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-banner-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-banner-1_0" width="1" height="1" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="6" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom; width: 300px; height: 250px;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><hr class="clear"><div class="content-ad-wrap"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-115"></span><span class="ezoic-ad box-4 box-4115 adtester-container adtester-container-115" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-box-4" style="min-height: 250px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-box-4-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 300px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CIerrLr-pPQCFTEB-QAd25gONQ"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-4_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 300px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-4_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="300" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="7" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span></div><hr class="clear"><h2>Why Should Small Businesses Be Concerned With Cyber Security?</h2><p>I know what youre thinking. Youre thinking that your business is so small, nobody would ever want to hack it.</p><p>Its easy to think that a small business would never have to deal with cyber security issues. Makes sense, right? Usually when you hear about a company being hacked, its a major brand like Target or Sony.</p><p>But these arent the only targets.</p><p>It may sound hard to believe, but hackers target small businesses too. You just dont hear about it because the media isnt going to report on hacks involving small businesses. There are several reasons why a hacker might go after a small business</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad1" id="quads-ad1" style="float:none;margin:3px 0;text-align:center"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-116"></span><span class="ezoic-ad medrectangle-4 medrectangle-4116 adtester-container adtester-container-116" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4" style="min-height: 400px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4-0" ezaw="580" ezah="400" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 400px; min-width: 580px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CJjBzbT-pPQCFaYW-QAdv6UDcw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4_0" width="580" height="400" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="8" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><h3>Small Businesses Dont Take Cyber Security Seriously</h3><p>Lets face it. Most small business owners dont take cyber security seriously. They think that theyre too small to get a hackers attention.</p><p>However, this is one of the main reasons why a small business might get hacked. Hackers know that most small business owners dont invest in cyber security.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad11" id="quads-ad11" style="float:none;margin:3px"><span id="SBT_Inline_affiliate_widget" class="SBT_Inline_affiliate_widget"></span></div><p>Why? Because small business owners tend to think they have nothing worth stealing. This makes them an easy target.</p><p>Chances are, you <em>do</em> have something that hackers want: customer payment information. That brings me to my next point</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad2" id="quads-ad2" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-158"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-1 leader-1158 adtester-container adtester-container-158" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-1" style="min-height: 400px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-1-0" ezaw="580" ezah="400" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 400px; min-width: 580px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CMSj5Lf-pPQCFbkW-QAdVb4GfA"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-1_0" width="580" height="400" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="9" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><h3>You Have Information That Hackers Want</h3><p>Your business may not be as big as Target or Starbucks  but it doesnt matter. You do take payment for your products and services, right? That means you have something that hackers want. You have your customers payment information. You have your employees information.</p><p>The Council of Better Business Bureaus found that <a href="http://tech.co/should-small-businesses-be-paying-more-attention-to-cyber-security-2016-10" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">7.4 percent of small business owners</a> have been defrauded. As a business owner, you have customer and employee information. This information is as valuable as gold to hackers. If your system isnt secure, these hackers could have access to payment information and social security numbers. Its your job to make sure that this information is protected.</p><h2>How to Protect Your Small Business Against A Cyber Attack</h2><p>Okay, so Ive showed you that being a small business doesnt necessarily mean that you cant get hacked. But if youre smart  and I know you are  youre probably wondering how you can protect your companys information. Thats what the next section of this post is about.</p><h3>Get Cyber Security Insurance</h3><p>Insurance! Its not just for your car, house or medical bills. You can also get insurance for your business. As a matter of fact, every company should carry some type of business insurance.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad3" id="quads-ad3" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-159"></span><span class="ezoic-ad large-mobile-banner-1 large-mobile-banner-1159 adtester-container adtester-container-159 ezoic-ad-adaptive" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1"><span class="ezoic-ad large-mobile-banner-1 large-mobile-banner-1-multi-159 adtester-container adtester-container-159" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1-0" ezaw="290" ezah="250" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 290px;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CN3gqLr-pPQCFbMH-QAdH3wNTg"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 250px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="250" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="a" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><span class="ezoic-ad large-mobile-banner-1 large-mobile-banner-1-multi-159 adtester-container adtester-container-159" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1-0_1" ezaw="290" ezah="250" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 290px;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CK3Cpbr-pPQCFUcJ-QAd7ZQLog"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_1__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 250px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_1" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="250" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="b" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><style>.large-mobile-banner-1-multi-159{border:none!important;display:block!important;float:none!important;line-height:0;margin-bottom:20px!important;margin-left:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-top:20px!important;min-height:250px;min-width:250px;padding:0;text-align:center!important}</style></span><hr class="clear"></div><p>But, there is also cyber security insurance. If youre a small business, you need this.</p><p>Sure, we all hope that security breaches wont happen. But hope isnt good enough. You need to make sure your business is covered.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad10" id="quads-ad10" style="float:none;margin:3px"><span id="SBT_Inline_adslot" class="SBT_Inline_Native_ad"></span></div><p>Cyber liability insurance is designed to protect your business from various cyber security threats. If there is a security breach, and your company is held liable, you may end up having to pay out tons of money in a lawsuit. This can cripple most small businesses.</p><p>If you have cyber liability insurance, you wont have to worry about this. If you buy the right type of insurance, your legal costs will be covered.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad4" id="quads-ad4" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-160"></span><hr class="clear"></div><h3>Develop A Password Strategy</h3><p>Many cyber security attacks happen because the passwords your employees use are way too simple. If your team isnt educated, its possible that theyre using passwords that are way too easy to hack.</p><p>It happens all the time.</p><p>Thats why you need to <a href="http://lifehacker.com/four-methods-to-create-a-secure-password-youll-actually-1601854240" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">implement an effective password strategy</a>. You may not be able to stop every single attack, but you can certainly slow down a persistent hacker. If your system isnt easy to hack, it could discourage the attacker. They will move on to another small business owner who isnt as smart as you are!</p><p>Fortunately, this is pretty easy.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad5" id="quads-ad5" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-161"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-3 leader-3161 adtester-container adtester-container-161" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-3" style="min-height: 90px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-3-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 90px; min-width: 728px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CLujqrr-pPQCFYz7ZAodwogPig"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-3_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-3_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-3_0" width="728" height="90" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="c" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><p>You should make sure that your team members are required to create passwords that include a combination of uppercase and lowercase letters, along with numbers and symbols. Yes, I know this might be a pain, but the security your company will have is worth it. Also, you should require your employees to reset their passwords at least once a month.</p><h3>Use Virtual Data Rooms (VDR)</h3><p>Virtual data rooms are a great way to <a href="http://www.securedocs.com/blog/virtual-data-room-information" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">keep your companys information secure</a>. They make it easier for your employees to share sensitive data.</p><p>A virtual data room is an online repository where your company can store data. Theyre usually used with financial transactions. Its very hard for a hacker to get to information that is stored in a VDR.</p><p>There are many types of information that a company might store in a VDR:</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad6" id="quads-ad6" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-610"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-2 leader-2610 adtester-container adtester-container-610" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-2" style="min-height: 250px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-2-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 300px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CJ-hnrb-pPQCFdwT-QAdwzUGZw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-2_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 300px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-2_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="300" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="d" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><ul><li>Financial information</li><li>Legal documentation</li><li>Tax paperwork</li><li>Intellectual property information</li></ul><p>VDRs are a great way to ensure that your sensitive information is being kept safe.</p><h3>Speak With An Expert</h3><p>Yes, I know you dont want to do it. But you should. Paying an IT security consultant might seem to be a little expensive. But its a <a href="http://intelligent-defense.softwareadvice.com/questions-to-ask-when-hiring-security-consultants-0314/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">great investment</a>.</p><p>If your house sprung a leak and water was building up in your kitchen, would you try to fix it yourself? Probably not. You would probably call a plumber, right?</p><p>Why? Because if youre like most of us, you dont know the first thing about plumbing. The same principle applies to IT security.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad7" id="quads-ad7" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-611"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-4 leader-4611 adtester-container adtester-container-611" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-4" style="min-height: 280px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-4-0" ezaw="336" ezah="280" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 280px; min-width: 336px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CNTZrLr-pPQCFSsB-QAdRoQENw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-4_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 336px; height: 280px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-4_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="336" height="280" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="e" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><p>If youre concerned about cyber security, you should consider speaking with an IT security expert. An IT security consultant can take a look at your business and determine the best course of action when it comes to protecting it from cyber attacks.</p><p>An IT security consultant can identify areas where your company is vulnerable to cyber attacks. They can make recommendations that will help you keep your business safe. When it comes to cyber security, you can never be too careful. If its in your budget, hire an expert. Youll be glad you did.</p><h3>Beware Of Internal Threats</h3><p>This may be a surprise, but most of the cyber security issues that happen are the result of someone inside the company. Its not something most business owners want to think about, but its totally true.</p><p>Heres a hard truth: <a href="https://smallbiztrends.com/2016/06/cyber-security-strategies.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">55 percent of all cyber attacks</a> come from inside the organization. 31.5 percent are done by malicious employees. 23.5 percent are done by company insiders who mistakenly leave the company vulnerable to an attack.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad8" id="quads-ad8" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-612"></span><span class="ezoic-ad mobile-leaderboard-1 mobile-leaderboard-1612 adtester-container adtester-container-612" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1" style="min-height: 90px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 90px; min-width: 728px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CMeexrf-pPQCFUUB-QAdL60BGw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1_0" width="728" height="90" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="f" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"><span class="final_injected_ad"></span></div><p>Protecting your company means looking within the organization. Its easy to assume that a cyber attack is going to come from an outside force. But its not true. You have to focus on the people inside your company just as much as people outside your company.</p><p>Make sure that you are keeping an eye on your authorization requirements. Be careful when youre deciding which employees should have access to sensitive data. This will help you prevent internal hacks.</p><p>Dont feel guilty for watching your employees activities; as the owner of your business, its your duty to ensure that you and your team are being protected. I get it. You dont want to micromanage. The key is to find the balance between being safe and being big brother. Its different for every company, but if you work at it, you will find that balance.</p><h2>Summing It All Up</h2><p>If youre a small business owner, you need to take your cyber security seriously. Dont assume that your company isnt a target just because youre not a big business.</p><p>You owe it to yourself, your employees and your customers to make sure that your business is secure. Preventing cyber attacks should be one of your top priorities. If you take the right steps, you wont have to worry about endangering your business.</p><p><small><em><a href="https://www.shutterstock.com/pic-507108913/stock-photo-hooded-computer-hacker-stealing-information-with-laptop.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Hacker</a> Photo via Shutterstock</em></small>

Here's how to protect your small business against a cyber attack","breadcrumb":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#breadcrumb"},"inLanguage":"en-US","potentialAction":[{"@type":"ReadAction","target":["https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html"]}]},{"@type":"BreadcrumbList","@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#breadcrumb","itemListElement":[{"@type":"ListItem","position":1,"name":"The Most Effective Ways To Protect Your Small Business From Cyber Attacks"}]},{"@type":["Article","NewsArticle"],"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#article","isPartOf":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#webpage"},"author":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#/schema/person/a08ac3acef91b65ea6a24e071bf9e67a"},"headline":"The Most Effective Ways To Protect Your Small Business From Cyber Attacks","datePublished":"2017-01-13T13:30:20+00:00","dateModified":"2021-04-13T13:07:41+00:00","mainEntityOfPage":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#webpage"},"wordCount":1486,"publisher":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#organization"},"image":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/how-to-protect-your-small-business-against-a-cyber-attack.html#primaryimage"},"thumbnailUrl":"https://media.smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/shutterstock_507108913.jpg","articleSection":["Technology Trends"],"inLanguage":"en-US","copyrightYear":"2017","copyrightHolder":{"@id":"https://smallbiztrends.com/#organization"},"articleBody":"Okay, I\u2019m going to start with a question. What would happen if a hacker decided to launch a cyber attack against your business? Would they be successful? Would they easily gain access to your company\u2019s sensitive information? Or would their attempt fall flat? Believe it or not, cyber security isn\u2019t just a concern for large businesses. It\u2019s something that small business owners need to pay attention to. Consider these statistics about Small Business Security: 43 percent of cyber attacks target small business. Only 14 percent of small businesses rate their ability to mitigate cyber risks, vulnerabilities and attacks as highly effective. 60 percent of small companies go out of business within six months of a cyber attack. 48 percent of data security breaches are caused by acts of malicious intent. Human error or system failure account for the rest. If you\u2019re a small business owner, you can\u2019t ignore these statistics. You don\u2019t want your business to suffer because you didn\u2019t take the appropriate steps to protect it. You have worked way too hard to allow your company to be threatened by a\u00a0hacker, right?\u00a0In this post, you will learn why it\u2019s important to focus on cyber security. You will also learn how you can protect your business. Why Should Small Businesses Be Concerned With Cyber Security? I know what you\u2019re thinking. You\u2019re thinking that your business is so small, nobody would ever want to hack it. It\u2019s easy to think that a small business would never have to deal with cyber security issues. Makes sense, right? Usually when you hear about a company being hacked, it\u2019s a major brand like Target or Sony. But these aren\u2019t the only targets. It may sound hard to believe, but hackers target small businesses too. You just don\u2019t hear about it because the media isn\u2019t going to report on hacks involving small businesses. There are several reasons why a hacker might go after a small business... Small Businesses Don\u2019t Take Cyber Security Seriously Let\u2019s face it. Most small business owners don\u2019t take cyber security seriously. They think that they\u2019re too small to get a hacker\u2019s attention. However, this is one of the main reasons why a small business might get hacked. Hackers know that most small business owners don\u2019t invest in cyber security. Why? Because small business owners tend to think they have nothing worth stealing. This makes them an easy target. Chances are, you do have something that hackers want: customer payment information. That brings me to my next point... You Have Information That Hackers Want Your business may not be as big as Target or Starbucks ... but it doesn\u2019t matter. You do take payment for your products and services, right? That means you have something that hackers want. You have your customers\u2019 payment information. You have your employees' information. The Council of Better Business Bureaus found that 7.4 percent of small business owners have been defrauded. As a business owner, you have customer and employee information. This information is as valuable as gold to hackers. If your system isn\u2019t secure, these hackers could have access to payment information and social security numbers. It\u2019s your job to make sure that this information is protected. How to Protect Your Small Business Against A Cyber Attack Okay, so I\u2019ve showed you that being a small business doesn\u2019t necessarily mean that you can\u2019t get hacked. But if you\u2019re smart --- and I know you are --- you\u2019re probably wondering how you can protect your company\u2019s information. That\u2019s what the next section of this post is about. Get Cyber Security Insurance Insurance! It\u2019s not just for your car, house or medical bills. You can also get insurance for your business. As a matter of fact, every company should carry some type of business insurance. But, there is also cyber security insurance. If you\u2019re a small business, you need this. Sure, we all hope that security breaches won\u2019t happen. But hope isn\u2019t good enough. You need to make sure your business is covered. Cyber liability insurance is designed to protect your business from various cyber security threats. If there is a security breach, and your company is held liable, you may end up having to pay out tons of money in a lawsuit. This can cripple most small businesses. If you have cyber liability insurance, you won\u2019t have to worry about this. If you buy the right type of insurance, your legal costs will be covered. Develop A Password Strategy Many cyber security attacks happen because the passwords your employees use are way too simple. If your team isn\u2019t educated, it\u2019s possible that they\u2019re using passwords that are way too easy to hack. It happens all the time. That\u2019s why you need to implement an effective password strategy. You may not be able to stop every single attack, but you can certainly slow down a persistent hacker. If your system isn\u2019t easy to hack, it could discourage the attacker. They will move on to another small business owner who isn\u2019t as smart as you are! Fortunately, this is pretty easy. You should make sure that your team members are required to create passwords that include a combination of uppercase and lowercase letters, along with numbers and symbols. Yes, I know this might be a pain, but the security your company will have is worth it. Also, you should require your employees to reset their passwords at least once a month. Use Virtual Data Rooms (VDR) Virtual data rooms are a great way to keep your company\u2019s information secure. They make it easier for your employees to share sensitive data. A virtual data room is an online repository where your company can store data. They\u2019re usually used with financial transactions. It\u2019s very hard for a hacker to get to information that is stored in a VDR. There are many types of information that a company might store in a VDR: Financial information Legal documentation Tax paperwork Intellectual property information VDR\u2019s are a great way to ensure that your sensitive information is being kept safe. Speak With An Expert Yes, I know you don\u2019t want to do it. But you should. Paying an IT security consultant might seem to be a little expensive. But it\u2019s a great investment. If your house sprung a leak and water was building up in your kitchen, would you try to fix it yourself? Probably not. You would probably call a plumber, right? Why? Because if you\u2019re like most of us, you don\u2019t know the first thing about plumbing. The same principle applies to IT security. If you\u2019re concerned about cyber security, you should consider speaking with an IT security expert. An IT security consultant can take a look at your business and determine the best course of action when it comes to protecting it from cyber attacks. An IT security consultant can identify areas where your company is vulnerable to cyber attacks. They can make recommendations that will help you keep your business safe. When it comes to cyber security, you can never be too careful. If it\u2019s in your budget, hire an expert. You\u2019ll be glad you did. Beware Of Internal Threats This may be a surprise, but most of the cyber security issues that happen are the result of someone inside the company. It\u2019s not something most business owners want to think about, but it\u2019s totally true. Here\u2019s a hard truth: 55 percent of all cyber attacks come from inside the organization. 31.5 percent are done by malicious employees. 23.5 percent are done by company insiders who mistakenly leave the company vulnerable to an attack. Protecting your company means looking within the organization. It\u2019s easy to assume that a cyber attack is going to come from an outside force. But it\u2019s not true. You have to focus on the people inside your company just as much as people outside your company. Make sure that you are keeping an eye on your authorization requirements. Be careful when you\u2019re deciding which employees should have access to sensitive data. This will help you prevent \u201cinternal hacks.\u201d Don\u2019t feel guilty for watching your employees\u2019 activities; as the owner of your business, it\u2019s your duty to ensure that you and your team are being protected. I get it. You don\u2019t want to micromanage. The key is to find the balance between being safe and being big brother. It\u2019s different for every company, but if you work at it, you will find that balance. Summing It All Up If you\u2019re a small business owner, you need to take your cyber security seriously. Don\u2019t assume that your company isn\u2019t a target just because you\u2019re not a big business. You owe it to yourself, your employees and your customers to make sure that your business is secure. Preventing cyber attacks should be one of your top priorities. If you take the right steps, you won\u2019t have to worry about endangering your business. class="clear"></div></div></div><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-178"></span><hr class="clear"><span class="full-span-featured-image"><img width="850" height="476" Here's how to protect your small business against a cyber attack" ezimgfmt="rs rscb12 src ng ngcb12" loading="eager" srcset="" sizes=""></span><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-179"></span><span class="ezoic-ad box-3 box-3179 adtester-container adtester-container-179" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-box-3" style="min-height: 90px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-box-3-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; min-height: 90px; min-width: 728px;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CPvDxrf-pPQCFYfqZAod7nkLjA"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-3_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-3_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-3_0" width="728" height="90" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="3" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"><div class="entry"><div class="entry-wrap"><p>Okay, Im going to start with a question.</p><p>What would happen if a hacker decided to launch a cyber attack against your business? Would they be successful? Would they easily gain access to your companys sensitive information? Or would their attempt fall flat?</p><p>Believe it or not, cyber security isnt just a concern for large businesses. Its something that small business owners need to pay attention to.</p><p>Consider these <a href="https://smallbiztrends.com/2017/01/cyber-security-statistics-small-business.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">statistics about Small Business Security</a>:</p><ul><li>43 percent of cyber attacks target small business.</li><li>Only 14 percent of small businesses rate their ability to mitigate cyber risks, vulnerabilities and attacks as highly effective.</li><li>60 percent of small companies go out of business within six months of a cyber attack.</li><li>48 percent of data security breaches are caused by acts of malicious intent. Human error or system failure account for the rest.</li></ul><p>If youre a small business owner, you cant ignore these statistics. You dont want your business to suffer because you didnt take the appropriate steps to protect it.</p><p>You have worked way too hard to allow your company to be threatened by a&nbsp;hacker, right?&nbsp;In this post, you will learn why its important to focus on cyber security. You will also learn how you can protect your business.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad9" id="quads-ad9" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-106"></span><span class="ezoic-ad banner-1 banner-1106 adtester-container adtester-container-106" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-banner-1" style="min-height: 280px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-banner-1-0" ezaw="336" ezah="280" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 280px; min-width: 336px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CIiDsbb-pPQCFQzcWwodfpMDzQ"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-banner-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-banner-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-banner-1_0" width="1" height="1" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="6" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom; width: 300px; height: 250px;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><hr class="clear"><div class="content-ad-wrap"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-115"></span><span class="ezoic-ad box-4 box-4115 adtester-container adtester-container-115" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-box-4" style="min-height: 250px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-box-4-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 300px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CIerrLr-pPQCFTEB-QAd25gONQ"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-4_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 300px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-box-4_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="300" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="7" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span></div><hr class="clear"><h2>Why Should Small Businesses Be Concerned With Cyber Security?</h2><p>I know what youre thinking. Youre thinking that your business is so small, nobody would ever want to hack it.</p><p>Its easy to think that a small business would never have to deal with cyber security issues. Makes sense, right? Usually when you hear about a company being hacked, its a major brand like Target or Sony.</p><p>But these arent the only targets.</p><p>It may sound hard to believe, but hackers target small businesses too. You just dont hear about it because the media isnt going to report on hacks involving small businesses. There are several reasons why a hacker might go after a small business</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad1" id="quads-ad1" style="float:none;margin:3px 0;text-align:center"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-116"></span><span class="ezoic-ad medrectangle-4 medrectangle-4116 adtester-container adtester-container-116" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4" style="min-height: 400px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4-0" ezaw="580" ezah="400" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 400px; min-width: 580px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CJjBzbT-pPQCFaYW-QAdv6UDcw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-medrectangle-4_0" width="580" height="400" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="8" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><h3>Small Businesses Dont Take Cyber Security Seriously</h3><p>Lets face it. Most small business owners dont take cyber security seriously. They think that theyre too small to get a hackers attention.</p><p>However, this is one of the main reasons why a small business might get hacked. Hackers know that most small business owners dont invest in cyber security.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad11" id="quads-ad11" style="float:none;margin:3px"><span id="SBT_Inline_affiliate_widget" class="SBT_Inline_affiliate_widget"></span></div><p>Why? Because small business owners tend to think they have nothing worth stealing. This makes them an easy target.</p><p>Chances are, you <em>do</em> have something that hackers want: customer payment information. That brings me to my next point</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad2" id="quads-ad2" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-158"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-1 leader-1158 adtester-container adtester-container-158" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-1" style="min-height: 400px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-1-0" ezaw="580" ezah="400" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 400px; min-width: 580px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CMSj5Lf-pPQCFbkW-QAdVb4GfA"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-1_0" width="580" height="400" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="9" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><h3>You Have Information That Hackers Want</h3><p>Your business may not be as big as Target or Starbucks  but it doesnt matter. You do take payment for your products and services, right? That means you have something that hackers want. You have your customers payment information. You have your employees information.</p><p>The Council of Better Business Bureaus found that <a href="http://tech.co/should-small-businesses-be-paying-more-attention-to-cyber-security-2016-10" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">7.4 percent of small business owners</a> have been defrauded. As a business owner, you have customer and employee information. This information is as valuable as gold to hackers. If your system isnt secure, these hackers could have access to payment information and social security numbers. Its your job to make sure that this information is protected.</p><h2>How to Protect Your Small Business Against A Cyber Attack</h2><p>Okay, so Ive showed you that being a small business doesnt necessarily mean that you cant get hacked. But if youre smart  and I know you are  youre probably wondering how you can protect your companys information. Thats what the next section of this post is about.</p><h3>Get Cyber Security Insurance</h3><p>Insurance! Its not just for your car, house or medical bills. You can also get insurance for your business. As a matter of fact, every company should carry some type of business insurance.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad3" id="quads-ad3" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-159"></span><span class="ezoic-ad large-mobile-banner-1 large-mobile-banner-1159 adtester-container adtester-container-159 ezoic-ad-adaptive" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1"><span class="ezoic-ad large-mobile-banner-1 large-mobile-banner-1-multi-159 adtester-container adtester-container-159" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1-0" ezaw="290" ezah="250" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 290px;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CN3gqLr-pPQCFbMH-QAdH3wNTg"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 250px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="250" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="a" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><span class="ezoic-ad large-mobile-banner-1 large-mobile-banner-1-multi-159 adtester-container adtester-container-159" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1-0_1" ezaw="290" ezah="250" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 290px;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CK3Cpbr-pPQCFUcJ-QAd7ZQLog"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_1__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 250px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-large-mobile-banner-1_1" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="250" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="b" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><style>.large-mobile-banner-1-multi-159{border:none!important;display:block!important;float:none!important;line-height:0;margin-bottom:20px!important;margin-left:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-top:20px!important;min-height:250px;min-width:250px;padding:0;text-align:center!important}</style></span><hr class="clear"></div><p>But, there is also cyber security insurance. If youre a small business, you need this.</p><p>Sure, we all hope that security breaches wont happen. But hope isnt good enough. You need to make sure your business is covered.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad10" id="quads-ad10" style="float:none;margin:3px"><span id="SBT_Inline_adslot" class="SBT_Inline_Native_ad"></span></div><p>Cyber liability insurance is designed to protect your business from various cyber security threats. If there is a security breach, and your company is held liable, you may end up having to pay out tons of money in a lawsuit. This can cripple most small businesses.</p><p>If you have cyber liability insurance, you wont have to worry about this. If you buy the right type of insurance, your legal costs will be covered.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad4" id="quads-ad4" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-160"></span><hr class="clear"></div><h3>Develop A Password Strategy</h3><p>Many cyber security attacks happen because the passwords your employees use are way too simple. If your team isnt educated, its possible that theyre using passwords that are way too easy to hack.</p><p>It happens all the time.</p><p>Thats why you need to <a href="http://lifehacker.com/four-methods-to-create-a-secure-password-youll-actually-1601854240" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">implement an effective password strategy</a>. You may not be able to stop every single attack, but you can certainly slow down a persistent hacker. If your system isnt easy to hack, it could discourage the attacker. They will move on to another small business owner who isnt as smart as you are!</p><p>Fortunately, this is pretty easy.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad5" id="quads-ad5" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-161"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-3 leader-3161 adtester-container adtester-container-161" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-3" style="min-height: 90px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-3-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 90px; min-width: 728px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CLujqrr-pPQCFYz7ZAodwogPig"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-3_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-3_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-3_0" width="728" height="90" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="c" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><p>You should make sure that your team members are required to create passwords that include a combination of uppercase and lowercase letters, along with numbers and symbols. Yes, I know this might be a pain, but the security your company will have is worth it. Also, you should require your employees to reset their passwords at least once a month.</p><h3>Use Virtual Data Rooms (VDR)</h3><p>Virtual data rooms are a great way to <a href="http://www.securedocs.com/blog/virtual-data-room-information" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">keep your companys information secure</a>. They make it easier for your employees to share sensitive data.</p><p>A virtual data room is an online repository where your company can store data. Theyre usually used with financial transactions. Its very hard for a hacker to get to information that is stored in a VDR.</p><p>There are many types of information that a company might store in a VDR:</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad6" id="quads-ad6" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-610"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-2 leader-2610 adtester-container adtester-container-610" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-2" style="min-height: 250px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-2-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 250px; min-width: 300px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CJ-hnrb-pPQCFdwT-QAdwzUGZw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-2_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 300px; height: 250px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-2_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="300" height="250" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="d" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><ul><li>Financial information</li><li>Legal documentation</li><li>Tax paperwork</li><li>Intellectual property information</li></ul><p>VDRs are a great way to ensure that your sensitive information is being kept safe.</p><h3>Speak With An Expert</h3><p>Yes, I know you dont want to do it. But you should. Paying an IT security consultant might seem to be a little expensive. But its a <a href="http://intelligent-defense.softwareadvice.com/questions-to-ask-when-hiring-security-consultants-0314/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">great investment</a>.</p><p>If your house sprung a leak and water was building up in your kitchen, would you try to fix it yourself? Probably not. You would probably call a plumber, right?</p><p>Why? Because if youre like most of us, you dont know the first thing about plumbing. The same principle applies to IT security.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad7" id="quads-ad7" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-611"></span><span class="ezoic-ad leader-4 leader-4611 adtester-container adtester-container-611" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-leader-4" style="min-height: 280px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-leader-4-0" ezaw="336" ezah="280" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 280px; min-width: 336px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CNTZrLr-pPQCFSsB-QAdRoQENw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-4_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none; display: inline-block; width: 336px; height: 280px;"><iframe frameborder="0" src="https://dcfa28b52d1a1d43bdcc57faed6344ff.safeframe.googlesyndication.com/safeframe/1-0-38/html/container.html" id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-leader-4_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" width="336" height="280" data-is-safeframe="true" sandbox="allow-forms allow-popups allow-popups-to-escape-sandbox allow-same-origin allow-scripts allow-top-navigation-by-user-activation" allow="attribution-reporting" data-google-container-id="e" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"></div><p>If youre concerned about cyber security, you should consider speaking with an IT security expert. An IT security consultant can take a look at your business and determine the best course of action when it comes to protecting it from cyber attacks.</p><p>An IT security consultant can identify areas where your company is vulnerable to cyber attacks. They can make recommendations that will help you keep your business safe. When it comes to cyber security, you can never be too careful. If its in your budget, hire an expert. Youll be glad you did.</p><h3>Beware Of Internal Threats</h3><p>This may be a surprise, but most of the cyber security issues that happen are the result of someone inside the company. Its not something most business owners want to think about, but its totally true.</p><p>Heres a hard truth: <a href="https://smallbiztrends.com/2016/06/cyber-security-strategies.html" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">55 percent of all cyber attacks</a> come from inside the organization. 31.5 percent are done by malicious employees. 23.5 percent are done by company insiders who mistakenly leave the company vulnerable to an attack.</p><div class="quads-location quads-ad8" id="quads-ad8" style="float:none;margin:3px"><hr class="clear"><span id="ezoic-pub-ad-placeholder-612"></span><span class="ezoic-ad mobile-leaderboard-1 mobile-leaderboard-1612 adtester-container adtester-container-612" data-ez-name="smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1" style="min-height: 90px;"><span id="div-gpt-ad-smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1-0" ezaw="728" ezah="90" style="position: relative; z-index: 0; padding: 0px; width: 100%; max-width: 1200px; min-height: 90px; min-width: 728px; margin-left: auto !important; margin-right: auto !important;" class="ezoic-ad ezfound" data-google-query-id="CMeexrf-pPQCFUUB-QAdL60BGw"><div id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1_0__container__" style="border: 0pt none;"><iframe id="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1_0" title="3rd party ad content" name="google_ads_iframe_/1254144,15550013/smallbiztrends_com-mobile-leaderboard-1_0" width="728" height="90" scrolling="no" marginwidth="0" marginheight="0" frameborder="0" allow="attribution-reporting" srcdoc="" data-google-container-id="f" style="border: 0px; vertical-align: bottom;" data-load-complete="true"></iframe></div></span></span><hr class="clear"><span class="final_injected_ad"></span></div><p>Protecting your company means looking within the organization. Its easy to assume that a cyber attack is going to come from an outside force. But its not true. You have to focus on the people inside your company just as much as people outside your company.</p><p>Make sure that you are keeping an eye on your authorization requirements. Be careful when youre deciding which employees should have access to sensitive data. This will help you prevent internal hacks.</p><p>Dont feel guilty for watching your employees activities; as the owner of your business, its your duty to ensure that you and your team are being protected. I get it. You dont want to micromanage. The key is to find the balance between being safe and being big brother. Its different for every company, but if you work at it, you will find that balance.</p><h2>Summing It All Up</h2><p>If youre a small business owner, you need to take your cyber security seriously. Dont assume that your company isnt a target just because youre not a big business.</p><p>You owe it to yourself, your employees and your customers to make sure that your business is secure. Preventing cyber attacks should be one of your top priorities. If you take the right steps, you wont have to worry about endangering your business.</p><p><small><em><a href="https://www.shutterstock.com/pic-507108913/stock-photo-hooded-computer-hacker-stealing-information-with-laptop.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Hacker</a> Photo via Shutterstock</em></small>
